yann uses dither
Dithering algorithms are used to give the illusion of color depth when the color palette of an image needs to be reduced. The error diffusion used in the dithering algorithm â[adds] the residual quantization error of a pixel onto is neighboring pixels, to be dealt with later.â To do that the algorithm is fed with a matrix of values. If applied on a gradient, each matrix, Floyd-Steinberg, partial burke, etc., alters the structure of the latter that becomes the canvas to showcase the beauty of the algorithm itself.

float r=0, s=0, z=0, angle=0, z2=0, angle2=0;
int size=300;
void setup() {
  size(800, 800, P3D);
  background(0);
}
void draw() {
  translate(width/2, height/2);
  background(0);
  noFill();
  ortho();
  //rotateY(radians(r));
  stroke(161,255,0);
  strokeWeight(5 );
  /*  angle+=.003;//controls wavy ondulation
   z=lerp( cos(angle), sin(angle), .2);
   angle2+=.005;//controls wavy ondulation
   z2=lerp( cos(angle2), sin(angle2), .001);*/  //nice one
  angle+=.003;//controls wavy ondulation
  z=lerp( cos(angle), sin(angle), .4);
  angle2+=.007;//controls wavy ondulation
  z2=lerp( cos(angle2), sin(angle2), .1);
  arcX(50, 0, z);
  //arcY(50, 0, z2);
  //arcY(100,0,z);
}
void arcX(float posX, float posY, float spin)
{

  pushMatrix();
  translate(-posX, posY);
  rotateY(map(spin, -1, 1, PI, -PI)+PI);
  
  arc(posX, posY, 200, 200, HALF_PI, PI+HALF_PI);
  
  popMatrix();
}
void arcY(float posX, float posY, float spin)
{

  pushMatrix();
  translate(posX, posY);
  rotateY(map(spin, -1, 1, -PI, PI));
  arc(posX, posY, 200, 200, HALF_PI, PI+HALF_PI);
  
  popMatrix();
}

boolean recordPDF = false;

int formResolution = 15;
float stepSize = 2;
float initRadius = 250;
float centerX, centerY;
float[] x = new float[formResolution];
float[] y = new float[formResolution];

boolean filled = false;
boolean freeze = false;


void setup() {
  // use full screen size 
  size(displayWidth, displayHeight);
  smooth();
randomSeed(1);

  centerX = mouseX;
  centerY = mouseY;
  float angle = radians(360/float(formResolution));
  float radius = initRadius * noise(0.5, 1.0);
  for (int i=0; i<formResolution; i++) {
    x[i] = cos(angle*i) * radius;
    y[i] = sin(angle*i) * radius;
  }
  background(255);
  translate(width/2,height/2);
  }


  void draw() {
    
   
    fill(0,10);
    noStroke();
     rect(0,0,width, height);
   
    // floating towards mouse position
    centerX += (mouseX-centerX) * .01;
    centerY += (mouseY-centerY) * .01;

    // calculate new points
    for (int i=0; i<formResolution; i++) {
      x[i] += random(-stepSize, stepSize);
      y[i] += random(-stepSize, stepSize);
      // ellipse(x[i],y[i],5,5);
    }

    strokeWeight(0.5);
    noFill();
    stroke(255,150);
    for (int i=0;i<12;i++){
      //scale(.3/i);
   circle(formResolution,centerX+sin(i)*initRadius,centerY+cos(i)*initRadius);
    } 
    
  }
  void circle(int FormRes, float cenX, float cenY){
  beginShape();
      // start controlpoint
      curveVertex(x[FormRes-1]+cenX, y[FormRes-1]+cenY);

      // only these points are drawn
      for (int i=0; i<FormRes; i++) {
        curveVertex(x[i]+cenX, y[i]+cenY);
      }
      curveVertex(x[0]+cenX, y[0]+cenY);

      // end controlpoint
      curveVertex(x[1]+cenX, y[1]+cenY);
      endShape();
  }

THEREFORE

I often go to Transmediale in Berlin, it isa festival for media philosophy and media art. They usually choose a topic for each year and they call experts to make presentation about it. Last march in our school HGK we also had a 4 day symposium about design. And there was a very interesting panel that was more horizontal. There were experts but they would sit together with the public and have open discussion regarding a topic. This format was very interesting and new for me and it was much more enriching than the normal talks. The guys doing this were: Brave New Alps, Decolonizing Design and Depatriarcalize (the spelling is wrong) Design. This said is not that you have to do that but maybe proposing alternative formats to the classic talk might be something interesting, could have any other form...

So I went to all your questions. As said for AI you can ask to Matteo Pasquinelli from the HfG in Karlsruhe, or Johannes Bruder and Felix Gerloff both form the IXDM the institute where I work. 
For the question "Wie sind 100 Franken am besten ins Gemeinwohl investiert?" I think you can really ask the people from my research project because it somehow is question that refers to Commoning you can ask Shintaro Miyazaki IXDM (thinking toys and games for Commoning) or Shusha Niederberger ZHDK (Creating commons)

What I miss are questions on the topic of post colonialism, gender and race. Other hot topics are: the blockchain and cryptocurrency, CRISPR and bioengineering, 

Than the question "Kann eine KuÌnstliche Intelligenz auch Empathie lernen?" I would also talk about ethics in machine intelligence, and for that you could invite the this researcher https://www.ted.com/talks/joy_buolamwini_how_i_m_fighting_bias_in_algorithms Joy Boulamwini form the MIT.

The two major classes during this five year  Und zwischend diesen beiden SÃ¤tzen springst du meiner Meinung nach von der ErklÃ¤rung, was ein Dither ist, zu deinem Projekt
I started coding at the age of 14 while enrolled at technical high school in La Spezia (Italy). The two major classes during this five year where informatics and electronics. At that time the resources at that school were pretty limited, and we were coding on computer only 2 hours per week. We were writing our algorithm on paper the whole week having the possibility to see if they were working in the 2 hours computer lab. I had no personal computer at the time, and the frustration of having such limited amount for coding on PC led me to lose interest in the discipline. In 2014 I started my project ERNNRNG. This project was the first attempt to reconnect with programming. At the beginning the project was about glitching images the âstandardâ way with text editor ad HEX editor. Soon I decided to âglitchâ the images in an analog way using the scanner. The project was also featured on some blogs, like the SFMOMA, Dazed and Confused and many more. The brief look into glitch community, and the beginning of my master in visual communication, led me to restart coding, using mainly processing and the java language.

Thank you for applying as a volunteer for transmediale 2017!

Following your online application, we would like to invite you to the first volunteer meeting, on January 13th, 2017 at 5 p.m. at the Podewil, KlosterstraÃe 68, 10179 Berlin.

At this meeting, you will receive an introduction to the festival program by Kristoffer Gansing (transmediale artistic director), Daphne Dragona (conference program curator), Inke Arns (âalien matterâ exhibition curator), and Sabrina KÃ¼rzinger (film and video program project manager), plus a first briefing on what volunteering for transmediale entails and what opportunities we offer. The transmediale team will also be introduced to you and there will be time for your questions.

Before the meeting, please make sure to double check your availability that you stated in your volunteer application. We will ask you to confirm it, and collect your availability for some extra dates (i.e. 23.-25.01 [daytime], 01.02 [daytime], 05.02 [daytime / evening], 6.-7.03 [daytime]). Your individual volunteer shifts will be assigned and communicated to you after the first meeting.

A second volunteer meeting, during which you will receive your initial job briefings, will be held at the festival venue, the Haus der Kulturen der Welt, at the end of January  (more details will follow).

We would like to remind you that all available volunteer shifts will be assigned on a first come - first serve basis, and that the attendance of both volunteer meetings is crucial in order to be considered. Exceptions can only be made for applicants not based in Berlin.

Please note that we are using Timecounts to manage shifts and communicate with you. Nevertheless you donÂ´t need to sign up or join the community hub.

We kindly ask you to confirm your presence at the meeting by replying to this email or writing to volunteers@transmediale.de by Tuesday evening (please let us know also if you wonÂ´t be able to join us).

If you have any further questions please donÂ´t hesitate to contact us.

Looking forward to meeting you all,

we decide to add a human player in the loop. He will called by the software to do the task in the real world, but instead of the model task he will do other things like, climb some steps, or do some exercises and so on...
The tasks for now are cleaning, cooking, administration and shopping. I know there is tons more, but for now it is only experimental.
they can either trade it for another task or decide to rest instead of working.
our first game/model looks at the distribution of labour inside commoning projects. We decided to develop a software that simulates the distribution of the labour giving the single agents/player the possibility to trade the task they recieved.
With the project we are gamifying the social structures of communal projects (wohngenosseschaft, communes, etc.), academia likes to call the act of living in such realities "commoning".
I'll explain the game in english because i'm to lazy to formulate the whole thing in german
